RATING: 6
Strengths: Cool scifi theme, great bang for the buck, very easy to learn, takes some time to master (replayability), lots of cool combos (replayability), fast play. The mechanics work very well within their limits.

Biggest gripe: Ultimately, and provided that both players' game mastery is on par, victory is decided by (draw) luck. 

Verdict: A great filler games for gamers, and a good way to introduce non-gamers/casual gamers to deck-builders/-cyclers. 

Still, people who like games to be won on meaningful decisions will get a) attracted and b) ultimately disappointed by this game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
While playing a different game at an open table at PAX 2016, we chatted up some folks nearby. One guy had just come in 8th at the Star Realms tourney, and was telling us about how great it was. His friend next to him offered to let us use his base deck to try it out. Explanation of the rules was simple given our past deck-builder experience and off we went! Chris bought the game and an expansion within an hour later!

Now that we have played it a handful of times more, my review: It's a standard deck builder, which I would compare to Marvel Legendary in that depending on the "faction" you buy/build up over the course of the game, there are positive interactions between the cards. I like the addition of bases and outposts to act as interesting modifiers to direct player interactions. Where it differs from M:L is you can set up, learn, and begin to play your first game of Star Realms in about 5 minutes. It is SO EASY to set up, play, and clean up, and can fit in your pocket! Also, right now a base set is like $14, or closer to $10-$12 on sale. Expansions are also cheap and plentiful.

I am eager to try a larger game. Right now we have only played two-player, but it must be really different to have to choose which competitors to attack or defend against with multiple opponents.

RATING: 9
2-player, competitive deck-building game. Similar to Ascension, players take turns adding cards to their deck from a "trading area" of five shared cards. Themed to space battles, with four distinct factions, each with their own theme and strategy. Victory requires complementary pairing of two or more factions, and each game is unique, due to the random nature of the cards available for purchase. Games between two players wrap up in less than thirty minutes.

RATING: 7
Star realms is a head to head combo deckbuilder. The design manages to cut out the middle fluff that I don't care for in most deckbuilders, the grind, while still giving you a chance to create a true engine and chain some amazing combos. The balance of the card sets and different factions is excellent allowing for many viable strategies for victory.

For a quick, combo chaining deckbuilding experience you can't find better than Star Realms (unless you're interested in playing with more than 2, but that comes with its own caveats...)

Hand management.

A super fast, super escalating game of belting one another with spaceships that has a wonderful dynamic of faction synergies. With four core factions, various abilities including stacking damage, bonus card purchases, enemy hand discards and extra card-draws, Star Realms almost always feels like it's flowing quickly and it a blast (hurr hurr) to play.

Friends of mine are testing their own variants with the game and it's so wonderfully primed for interesting custom-made game types, there's so much more mileage in this than the impressive breadth offered out of the box.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
What a great little deck builder that's incredibly reminiscent of Ascension: row of cards available to everyone, those cards are part of various factions, there are two currencies, and getting rid of cards can be a large part of the game. However, instead of just trying to gain abstract points, you're trying to destroy your opponent(s) and I think it makes for a more interesting game.

The other part of this game that I really enjoy is the fact that you can start playing for $15 and if you want to play with more, just add in another $15 deck of cards and you're ready to go. It's up to you how much you want to spend and how many people you want to play with, something I wish other games would even consider.

Given the price, it's definitely worth a purchase if you like either deck builders or sci-fi games.

RATING: 7.5
One of my personal favs to introduce to someone when there's just two of us sitting around. The setup time is under a minute at the rules can be taught during play which make it perfect for getting right into some action.

It's definitely very luck driven, a couple of good market reveals for your opponent can have you pretty much shafted for the game. But that really doesn't stop me from wanting to play or enjoying myself when I do. In a way, the luck helps the game be more approachable, as even a pro will get it handed to them when the deck just isn't in their favor.

And man is it satisfying to land those crazy huge combos!

After the Dominion deception, which is rated so highly and didn't get into it at all, i thought LCG's weren't my thing. Star realm proves the opposite and is twice the game Dominion is for me. The simple design without losing game depth, but increases game flow makes it quite genius. 

It's portable, setup in a minute, is quick flowing, exciting and there are many ways to win. Even my GF loves it, which surprised me! We both don't particularly like Sci-fi themes, but this one gets to us. We really feel we're battling with space ships. Nice artwork!  

Only the manual isn't clear with some minor details, although i think we figured most out ourselves. 

Will buy more sets for sure :-)

I do feel the Blob faction is a tad overpowered compared to the others, the more we play it, the more it becomes a race for the Blob cards. The challenge is to win with other strategies though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A very cool little game.  It is by no means deap, as you really only just draw cards and then play all of them with little importance to when.  And even the core deck building mechanic of the five purchasable cards is so random and limiting that any strategy will often crack when faced with the limited tactical purchase choices on any given turn.
All that said, the game is fun!  First, it's quick.  No fiddly, overly complex rules.  No difficult timing issues (well, it does matter when you play cards - some refer to your hand, which obviously doesn't include the cards you've already played - so timing makes a small part of play).  Obvious synergies. And second, it's cheap and portable.  Plus, with the Gambit expantion (arguably the least inovative expantion) you can even play solo and co-op.  
Very neat!

RATING: 8
Very light deck builder where basically your only meaningful choice each turn is which card(s) to buy from a selection of 5. That card then goes into your discard pile and has no effect on play until you reshuffle and hope to draw it, which I think is a bad mechanic.

Given that strategic and tactical options are minimal, it's a decent game. I like the artwork, it's very cheap to buy, and has it's own charm in a light, fun way.

Excellent value for money. A good buy for young teens.

RATING: 7
My friend was totally right to recommend this one - all that I want from a deck builder, no more, no less. Fast, balanced, never felt that the luck of the draw influenced play to much (especially since you are never going to play  only one game in a session :-)
Very very nice artwork, although frequently overlooked in the bustle of play.
Various strategies possible and competent.

Of course, as any small card game, wears out after some playing if you don't add expansions.

RATING: 10
It fills a similar niche as Magic the Gathering, by being a quick (15 minute) filler game, with direct combat in the style of a duel. The cheap price ($10) and lack of prep time makes it a lot better than any CCG for these purposes, especially since your opponent doesn't even need to bring anything. Just break this bad boy out at the lunch table and play with a friend, whether or not they've even heard of it, much less brought their own deck. Also, the graphic design as amazing.
